Calculating Radd in Inheritance: Mother and Uterine Brothers
Explains radd method with example of mother and uterine brothers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the final shares using the radd method for a case involving a mother and two uterine brothers, and apply the radd multiplier.

Core Idea
When surplus remains after fixed shares, radd returns it proportionally to all Quranic heirs except the spouse.

In Hanafi inheritance law, after distributing the fixed Quranic shares (fara'id), any surplus is returned to the heirs (except spouses) in proportion to their shares. This lesson walks through a classic example: a deceased leaves a mother and two uterine brothers. We will compute the radd by finding a multiplier and applying it to each heir's original share.

Guided Path
1
Identify heirs and their fard shares
List the heirs: mother (1/6) and two uterine brothers (1/3 combined). Express shares with a common denominator.
Uterine brothers are siblings sharing only the mother; they are Quranic heirs, not residuaries.
2
Calculate total fard shares and surplus
Add the fixed shares: 1/6 + 1/3 = 1/6 + 2/6 = 3/6 = 1/2. The surplus is 1 − 1/2 = 1/2.
Surplus exists because the total fard is less than the whole estate.
3
Determine radd multiplier
Divide the surplus by the total fixed shares: (1/2) ÷ (1/2) = 1.
The multiplier is 1, meaning each heir's share is doubled.
4
Apply multiplier to each heir
Multiply each heir's original share by (1 + multiplier) = 2. Mother: 1/6 × 2 = 2/6 = 1/3. Uterine brothers: 1/3 × 2 = 2/3 collectively.
The decimal method in the text uses base 100 for convenience.

Source Text

راد کا طریقہ
حاشیہ : ( پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) بیوی اور شوہر کو دوبارہ کچھ نہیں دیتے تھے۔ اور حضرت زید ہر حصے دار کو حصہ دے دیتے اور جو باقی بچا اس کو بیت المال میں جمع کر دیتے۔
Chapter of Radd. Number 7 3116) This report states that Hadrat Zayd ibn Thabit used to put the remaining property into the public treasury. He would not return it to the share holders. As-siham: plural of sahm, shares. The new method of Radd. The method of Radd with a calculator is that you keep the total of all the shares taken by the recipients, and by this you divide the amounts that remain. After division, the quotient will be one share for all the share holders. Afterwards, multiply this by each share, and all the share holders will receive their full share. Remember that the calculator always leaves out one penny, so later adjust by adding a penny. (Examples) How to redistribute the remaining amounts to the share holders again, understand through examples. First example: For example, the deceased left two uterine brothers and a mother. So the two uterine brothers will get one-third, i.e., 33.33 out of 100. And the mother will get one-sixth, i.e., 16.66. And 50 will remain. The brothers took 33.33 and the mother took 16.66, their total is 50. Now divide the remaining 50 by this 50, the quotient will be 1. Then multiply 1 by 16.66, so the mother will again get 16.66 as radd, and her total becomes 33.33. And multiply 1 by the brothers' share 33.33, so they will also get 33.33 again as radd, and their total out of 100 becomes 66.66. The problem will be as follows: deceased 100, (one share) 1 = 50:50, total of shares, two uterine brothers, mother, leftover 50, leftover as radd =, total share 50, 16.66, 33.33, +16.66, +33.33, 33.33, ← 66.66. Mother got radd, uterine brothers got radd. 16.66x1 = 16.66, 33.33×1 = 33.33. Method of Radd. Marginal note: (continued from previous page) They would not give anything again to wife and husband. And Hadrat Zayd would give each share holder his share, and what remained he would deposit in the public treasury.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamiri introduces the chapter on al-Radd (return of surplus) in inheritance law. The author first cites an athar (report) that Hadrat Zayd ibn Thabit, a prominent Companion and early authority on fara'id, would treat any surplus after distributing the fixed shares (fara'id) as belonging to the public treasury (bayt al-mal) and would not return it to the heirs. This was one of the early positions. However, the established Hanafi position (and the one explained here) is that the surplus is returned (radd) to the heirs proportionately, with the exception of the spouse (husband or wife), who does not participate in the return. The author then presents a practical method for calculating radd using a calculator, advising to keep track of the sum of the shares taken and dividing the surplus by that sum to obtain a multiplier, which is then applied to each heir's original share to determine the additional amount from radd. He also warns about calculator rounding errors. The first example illustrates this: a deceased leaves a mother (gets 1/6) and two uterine brothers (get 1/3 collectively). Total shares sum to 1/2 (50 out of 100). The surplus is also 1/2. Dividing surplus by total shares gives 1. So each heir's share is doubled via radd: mother ends with 1/3, brothers with 2/3. The marginal note reiterates that spouses are excluded from radd. The passage is educational, aiming to equip students with a straightforward computational technique for radd.

Key Terms
رد (radd): The return of surplus property to the Quranic heirs (except spouses) after their fixed shares are distributed, in proportion to their shares.
ماں شریک (ma shariq): Uterine brothers (brothers sharing only the mother). In Hanafi fara'id, they are a distinct category entitled to 1/3 if two or more.
سهام (siham): Plural of sahm, meaning shares, specifically the portions allocated to heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first example, after distributing the fard shares to the mother and two uterine brothers, what is the multiplier used to calculate the radd amount?
A) 0.5
B) 1
C) 2
D) 0.333

Key Takeaway
Radd returns surplus to heirs proportionally, using a multiplier derived from surplus divided by total fixed shares, ensuring the entire estate is distributed among the heirs (excluding spouses).

Radd Calculation: One Daughter and One Granddaughter
Faraid radd example with two female sharers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the radd distribution when two female sharers inherit and no male residuary exists.

Core Idea
When no 'asabah remains, the surplus returns to the sharers in proportion to their fixed shares.

In this lesson, we walk through a straightforward case of radd in Hanafi faraid. The heirs are a daughter and a granddaughter (through a son). Their fixed shares (1/2 and 1/6) total 2/3 of the estate, leaving a 1/3 surplus. Since there is no male agnatic heir, the surplus is returned to them in proportion to their original shares. The text uses a base of 100 to explain the arithmetic, but we will also show the method using the traditional asl al-mas'alah of 6.

Guided Path
1
Identify all heirs and their fixed shares
List the two heirs: daughter (1/2) and granddaughter (1/6). These are both Qur'anic heirs (fard).
Granddaughter's share is 1/6 to complete the two-thirds share when there is one daughter.
2
Express shares with a common denominator
Use denominator 6: daughter = 3/6, granddaughter = 1/6. Sum = 4/6, residue = 2/6.
The residue is the difference between the whole estate (1) and the sum of shares (4/6).
3
Determine the radd multiplier
Divide the residue (2/6) by the sum of shares (4/6). The multiplier is 0.5.
This multiplier represents the proportionate share of the surplus each heir receives relative to their original share.
4
Apply the multiplier to each share
Multiply each heir's share (in sixths) by 0.5: daughter: 3/6 × 0.5 = 1.5/6; granddaughter: 1/6 × 0.5 = 0.5/6.
Alternatively, using a base of 100 as in the text: daughter's 50 × 0.5 = 25, granddaughter's 16.66 × 0.5 = 8.33.
5
Calculate final shares
Add the radd portion to the original share: daughter: 3/6 + 1.5/6 = 4.5/6 = 75/100; granddaughter: 1/6 + 0.5/6 = 1.5/6 = 25/100.
The radd is distributed in proportion to the original shares, not equally.

Source Text

دوسری مثال میت نے ایک بیٹی اور ایک پوتی چھوڑی اس لئے بیٹی کو 100 میں سے آدھا 50 ملے گا۔ اور دو تہائی پوری کرنے کے لئے ہوتی کو چھٹا یعنی 100 میں سے 16.66 ملے گا۔ اور تمام حصوں کا مجموعہ 66.66 ہو جائے گا۔ اب 66.66 سے 33.33 میں تقسیم دیں تو ایک حصہ 0.5 نکل آئے گا۔ پھر 0.5 سے ہوتی کے حصے 16.66 میں ضرب دیں تو پوتی کورد میں سے 8.33 مل جائے گا اور مجموعہ 25 ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح 0.5 سے بیٹی کے حصے 50 میں ضرب دیں تو 25 ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ بیٹی کو بطور رد جائے گا۔ اور حصہ اور رد ملا کر مجموعہ 75 مل جائے گا۔ مسئلہ اس طرح بنے گا۔

Second example: The deceased left one daughter and one granddaughter. Therefore the daughter gets half, 50 out of 100. And to complete two-thirds, the granddaughter gets one-sixth, i.e. 16.66 out of 100. The total of shares becomes 66.66. Now divide 66.66 into 33.33, the quotient is 0.5. Then multiply 0.5 by the granddaughter's share 16.66, so the granddaughter gets 8.33 by way of radd, and the total becomes 25. Similarly, multiply 0.5 by the daughter's share 50, result 25, which goes to the daughter as radd. So share plus radd totals 75. The problem is set up as follows: Deceased: 100, One part = 0.5=33.33:66.66, Total of shares: One daughter: 50, Granddaughter: 16.66, Remaining: 33.33, +8.33, +25, 25 ← 75. Method of radd: 16.66×0.5=8.33, 50.00×0.5=25, 66.66, Remaining as radd, Total; Granddaughter receives radd: 8.33, One daughter receives radd: 25.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage presents a faraid example of radd (return of surplus) when the shares of the Qur'anic heirs do not exhaust the estate. The deceased leaves two female descendants: a daughter (who gets half as her prescribed share) and a granddaughter (who gets one-sixth to complete the two-thirds share prescribed for daughters when there is no son). However, the total of these shares is only 66.66 out of 100, leaving a residue of 33.33. Since there is no 'asabah (agnatic heir) to take the residue, the surplus is returned to the sharers in proportion to their shares. The method shown: divide the residue (33.33) by the sum of shares (66.66) to get the proportion (0.5), then multiply each heir's share by this proportion to find their additional portion from the radd. The granddaughter's radd is 8.33, making her total 25; the daughter's radd is 25, making her total 75. This follows the Hanafi rule that radd is given to all sharers except the spouse, who does not receive radd. Note that in this example, the granddaughter is treated as a sharer (not a residuary) because she is a descendant through the son, and she inherits alongside the daughter. The calculation uses a base of 100 for clarity, but actual inheritance works with the asl al-mas'alah.

Key Terms
رد (radd): Return of the surplus estate to the sharers (Qur'anic heirs) in proportion to their shares when there is no 'asabah.
پوتی (potti): Granddaughter (daughter of son) who inherits as a sharer in the absence of a son.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example with one daughter and one granddaughter, why does the granddaughter receive only 1/6 initially and not 1/2?
A) Because she is not a direct descendant
B) Because she is of a lower generation and her share is fixed at 1/6 when there is a daughter
C) Because the daughter excludes her from inheritance completely
D) Because the granddaughter is a residuary heir

Key Takeaway
In radd, the surplus is distributed among the sharers in the proportion of their fixed shares, using a common multiplier derived from the ratio of residue to total shares.

Radd Calculation: Two Daughters and Mother
Faraid example: radd for two daughters and mother

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the radd distribution when the heirs are two daughters and a mother, and explain why the mother receives radd.

Core Idea
When no 'asabah exists, surplus is returned proportionally to all sharers except the spouse.

In this lesson, we work through a classic Hanafi faraid example: the deceased leaves only two daughters and a mother. Their prescribed shares (2/3 and 1/6) sum to 5/6, leaving a surplus. Since there is no 'asabah, the surplus is returned to them by radd. We will follow the calculation step by step, using both fractions and decimals, and see how the mother—unlike a spouse—participates in the radd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their shares
List the heirs: two daughters (2/3 collectively) and mother (1/6). Convert to a common denominator (6): daughters 4/6, mother 1/6.
The shares are based on the Qur'an (Surah an-Nisa 4:11).
2
Sum the shares and find the residue
Add the shares: 4/6 + 1/6 = 5/6. The residue is 1/6 (the surplus).
If the sum equalled 6/6, no radd or awl would be needed.
3
Determine the radd proportion
Divide the residue by the total shares: (1/6) ÷ (5/6) = 1/5 = 0.2. This is the proportion of the surplus each share receives.
The proportion is applied to each individual share, not per heir.
4
Apply radd to each heir
Multiply each share by the proportion: daughters: 4/6 × 1/5 = 4/30 = 2/15; mother: 1/6 × 1/5 = 1/30.
These are the radd amounts added to their original shares.
5
Compute final shares
Add the radd to each original share: daughters: 4/6 + 2/15 = (20/30+4/30)=24/30=4/5=80%; mother: 1/6+1/30=6/30=1/5=20%.
The final distribution exhausts the estate (80%+20%=100%).

Third example: The deceased left two daughters and a mother. Therefore the daughters get two-thirds 66.66 out of 100. The mother gets one-sixth 16.66. Adding both shares gives 83.32. The remainder is 16.68. Now divide 83.32 into the mother's 16.66, quotient 0.200. Then multiply 0.200 by mother's 16.66, result 3.33 which goes to the mother as radd, total 19.99 i.e. 20. Multiply 0.200 by the daughters' share 66.66, result 13.33 which goes to the two daughters as radd, total shares 79.99 i.e. 80. The problem is set up as: Deceased: 100, Total of shares: Two daughters: 66.66, Mother: 16.66, One part = 0.200=83.32:16.68, Remaining: 16.68, +3.33, 19.99=, 66.66, +13.33, 79.99=, 83.32, Remaining as radd, Total; Mother receives radd: 16.66×0.200=3.33; Two daughters receive radd: 66.66×0.200=13.33. And set the calculation with a calculator.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This is another faraid example of radd (return of surplus). The deceased is survived by two daughters (who collectively take two-thirds) and a mother (who takes one-sixth). The total of these fixed shares is 83.32 out of 100, leaving 16.68 as surplus. Since there is no 'asabah, the surplus is returned to the sharers proportionally. The method: divide the surplus by the total shares to get the proportion (0.200), then multiply each share by this proportion. The mother's radd is 3.33, making her total approximately 20; the daughters' radd is 13.33, making their total approximately 80. The textbook rounds the numbers for simplicity. This illustrates the Hanafi rule that radd is given to all sharers including the mother (who is not excluded from radd). Note that the mother is a sharer and receives radd in addition to her prescribed share.

Key Terms
رد (radd): Return of surplus to sharers in proportion to their shares when no 'asabah exists.
ماں (maan): Mother of the deceased, a Qur'anic sharer who receives 1/6 when there are children.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third example, what is the proportion (حصہ) used to distribute the radd?
A) 0.5
B) 0.200
C) 0.166
D) 0.333

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, when the total shares do not exhaust the estate and there is no 'asabah, the surplus is returned to all non-spousal sharers in proportion to their prescribed shares.

The Killer Does Not Inherit: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with hadith proof on killer's deprivation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inheritance by a killer and explain how the hadith proves this deprivation.

Core Idea
The killer is completely barred from inheriting from the victim, whatever the type of killing.

This lesson addresses a fundamental rule in inheritance law: a person who causes the death of another cannot benefit from that death by inheriting. The Hanafi school, relying on a clear hadith, holds that the killer is deprived of any share, whether the killing was intentional or accidental. We will examine the ruling, the proof, and the scope of application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage carefully. What is the legal consequence for the killer regarding inheritance?
The ruling is a complete bar, not a reduction.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites a hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb. Identify the source books and the specific wording of the proof.
The key phrase is 'la yarith al-qatil shay'an'.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith explicitly indicate the ruling? What is the linguistic cue?
The negation is absolute and general.
4
Note the epistemological weight
The hadith is ahad (single-chain). How does the Hanafi school treat such a proof?
Though zanni al-thubut, its meaning (dalala) is qat'i, so it is binding.
5
Consider the scope and ikhtilaf
Does the bar apply to all types of killing? What is the mufta bihi position?
The mature position is that any killing causing death bars inheritance, even indirect or accidental.

محروم کا بیان ہے
[3230] (2) ولايرث القاتل من المقتول
قاتل مقتول کا وارث نہیں بنے گا۔
حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عمر بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده قال كان رسول الله الله ... وقال رسول الله للقاتل شيء وان لم يكن له وارث فوارثه اقرب الناس اليه ولا يرث القاتل شيئا (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب دیات الاعضاء ، ج ۲، ص ۲۷۸، نمبر ۴۵۶۴، کتاب الدیات رترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی ابطال میراث القاتل ، ج ۲، ص ۱۳۱، نمبر ۲۱۰۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قاتل وارث نہیں ہوگا۔
Statement of the deprived:
[3230] (2) The killer does not inherit from the killed.
The killer will not become the heir of the killed.
In the hadith: from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather: The Messenger of Allah said... and the Messenger of Allah said: 'The killer has no share [of inheritance]; and if he has no heir, then his nearest relative inherits from him, but the killer does not inherit anything.' (Abu Dawud, Book of Diyat, Chapter of Limb Diyat, vol. 2, p. 278, no. 4564; Tirmidhi, Book of Diyat, Chapter on abolishing inheritance of the killer, vol. 2, p. 131, no. 2109). From this hadith it is known that the killer will not inherit.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage presents a clear ruling from the Hanafi school: a person who kills the deceased is completely barred from inheriting from that victim. The ruling is supported by a marfu' hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb that explicitly states the killer inherits nothing. The text references the source in Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi. The Hanafi school applies this rule broadly, covering intentional killing (qatl 'amd), accidental killing (qatl khata'), and even indirect killing, although there is some ikhtilaf within the school regarding the extent. The ruling is based on the principle that the killer cannot benefit from the death he caused. The hadith also mentions that if the deceased has no heir, the next of kin inherits, but still not the killer. The authority weight here is from the hadith (Sunnah ahad), which is zanni al-thubut, but the ruling is accepted by consensus among the schools on the basic principle, with differences in details.

Key Terms
قاتل (qatil): The person who causes the death of the deceased, whether intentionally or accidentally.
مقتول (maqtul): The person who is killed, the victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the hadith cited in this lesson, what happens if the killer is the only relative of the deceased?
A) The killer inherits as the nearest relative
B) The killer inherits after paying diyah
C) The nearest relative other than the killer inherits
D) The estate goes to the state

Key Takeaway
A killer is completely barred from inheriting from the victim, as established by the clear wording of the hadith.

All disbelief is one religion for inheritance
Inter-madhhab dispute on cross-religion inheritance among non-Muslims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on inheritance between non-Muslims of different faiths and evaluate the opposing evidence using the principle that all kufr is one millah.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, all non-Muslims inherit from each other because they share one millah of disbelief.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools regarding inheritance between non-Muslims of different religions. The Hanafi position holds that all disbelief (kufr) constitutes a single millah, so a Christian can inherit from a Jew. The opposing view sees each non-Muslim religion as a separate millah barring cross-inheritance. We will analyze the proofs and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Identify the Hanafi claim: all disbelievers are one millah for inheritance. Note the athar from Sufyan al-Thawri: 'Islam is one religion and shirk is one religion.' Explain how this supports the Hanafi view.
The athar is a statement from a tabi'i, considered strong evidence in Hanafi usul.
2
Identify the opposing view and its evidence
State that some imams (especially Shafi‘i) hold that each non-Muslim religion is a separate millah. Cite the athar from al-Hasan al-Basri ('The Jew does not inherit from the Christian') and the hadith from Jabir ('People of two religions do not inherit from each other').
The hadith is stronger in transmission but its interpretation is disputed.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing evidence
Explain the Hanafi interpretation: the hadith refers to two religions meaning Islam vs. kufr, not different types of kufr. The athar from Sufyan is given priority because it comes from a more reliable chain and reflects the general rule.
Hanafis view the diversity of kufr as only branches, not separate religions for inheritance.
4
Determine the practical consequence and the mufta bihi
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Hanafi law a Christian inherits from a Jew; under the opposing view they do not. Conclude that the author and the Hanafi school adopt the position of a single millah for all kufr.
This is the mufta bihi view in the Hanafi madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[3231] (3) والكفر ملة واحدة يتوارث به اهله.
ہر قسم کا کفر ایک ملت ہے اس لئے کافر دوسرے کافر کا وارث ہوگا۔
یہودی کے رشتہ دار یہودی ہو تو وارث ہو گا ہی۔ لیکن یہودی کا رشتہ دار نصرانی یا مجوسی ہو تو وارث ہوگا یا نہیں تو اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ مصنف کی رائے ہے کہ نصرانی یا مجوسی یہودی کا وارث ہوگا۔ کافر چاہے یہودی ہو یا نصرانی ایک مذہب ہے یعنی کافر ہے۔ اس لئے وہ ایک دوسرے کے وارث ہوں گے (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ حدثنا سفيان الاسلام ملة والشرك ملة (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة، ۸۸ فی النصرانی سیث الیہودی والیہودی میث النصرانی، ج سادس، ص ۲۸۸، نمبر ۳۱۴۴۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ تمام کفر گویا کہ ایک مذہب ہے۔ اس لئے وہ ایک دوسرے کے وارث ہوں گے۔
بعض ائمہ کی رائے ہے کہ یہودی نصرانی کے اور نصرانی یہودی کے وارث نہیں ہوں گے۔
ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن الحسن قال لا يرث اليهودى النصراني ولا يرث النصراني اليهودي (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة، ۸۸ فی النصرانی سیٹ الیہودی والیہودی سرث النصرانی، ج سادس، ص ۲۸۷، نمبر ۳۱۴۴۳) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ایک دوسرے کے وارث نہیں ہوں گے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن جابر عن النبي لا الا الله قال لايتوارث اهل ملتین (د) ( ترمذی شریف ، باب لا يتوارث اهل ملتین ص ۳۱ نمبر ۲۱۰۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو مذہب والے ایک دوسرے کے وارث نہیں ہوں گے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے فرمایا قاتل کے لئے کوئی وراثت نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر اس کا کوئی وارث نہ ہو تو قریب کے لوگ اس کے وارث ہوں گے۔ اور قاتل کسی چیز کا وارث نہیں ہو گا (ب) حضرت سفیان نے فرمایا اسلام الگ دین ہے اور شرک الگ دین ہے (ج) حضرت حسن نے فرمایا یہودی نصرانی کا وارث نہیں ہوگا۔ اور نصرانی یہودی کا وارث نہیں ہو گا (1) حضور نے فرمایا دو دین والے ایک دوسرے کے وارث نہیں ہوں گے۔
[3231] (3) And disbelief (kufr) is one religion (millah); its people inherit from each other.
Every type of disbelief is one religion, therefore a disbeliever will inherit from another disbeliever.
If a Jew's relative is also Jewish, he will inherit of course. But if the Jew's relative is Christian or Magian, then there is disagreement about whether he inherits. The author's opinion is that a Christian or Magian will inherit from a Jew. A disbeliever, whether Jewish or Christian, is one religion, i.e., a disbeliever. Therefore they will inherit from each other. (2) There is proof in the athar: Sufyan narrated: 'Islam is one religion and shirk (polytheism) is one religion' (Ibn Abi Shayba, Kitab al-Nasrani yarith al-Yahudi ..., vol.6, p.288, no.31444). This athar shows that all kufr is essentially one religion, so they inherit from each other.
Some imams hold the opinion that a Jew does not inherit from a Christian, and a Christian does not inherit from a Jew.
Their proof is this athar: from al-Hasan who said: 'The Jew does not inherit from the Christian, nor does the Christian inherit from the Jew' (Ibn Abi Shayba, Kitab al-Nasrani yarith al-Yahudi ..., vol.6, p.287, no.31443). This athar states that they will not inherit from each other. (2) There is a hadith from Jabir from the Prophet (may peace be upon him) who said: 'People of two religions do not inherit from each other' (Tirmidhi, Chapter: People of two religions do not inherit, p.31, no.2108). This hadith indicates that people of two different religions do not inherit from each other.
Footnote: (a) The Prophet said: The killer has no inheritance; and if he has no heir, then his nearest relative inherits, and the killer will not inherit anything. (b) Sufyan said: Islam is a religion and shirk is a religion. (c) Hasan said: The Jew does not inherit from the Christian, nor the Christian from the Jew. (d) The Prophet said: People of two religions do not inherit from each other.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage deals with a significant inter-madhhab dispute regarding inheritance between non-Muslims of different faiths. The Hanafi position, as stated by the author, is that all types of kufr (disbelief) are considered one millah (religious community) for the purpose of inheritance. Thus, a Jew can inherit from a Christian, a Christian from a Magian, etc. The author cites an athar from Sufyan al-Thawri: 'Islam is one religion and shirk is one religion,' arguing that all non-Muslims are on the same side. The opposing view, attributed to some imams (likely the Shafi'i school), is that each non-Muslim religion is a separate millah, so inheritance does not cross religious lines. They cite an athar from al-Hasan al-Basri that a Jew does not inherit from a Christian, and also the famous hadith 'People of two religions do not inherit from each other' (reported by Tirmidhi). The author includes these proofs in the text, presenting the dispute fairly. The Hanafi interpretation of the hadith is that the two religions refer to Islam vs. non-Islam, not to different types of kufr. Thus, for Hanafis, all kufr is one side, and Islam is the opposite side. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in a Hanafi court, a Christian can inherit from a Jewish relative, whereas in Shafi'i law, they would not. The author's opinion is clearly in favor of the Hanafi position. The hashia at the end summarizes the proofs. This passage exemplifies the Hanafi method of using rational grouping (millah) and athar to support their position.

Key Terms
ملة (millah): A religious community or affiliation; used to determine inheritance between different faiths.
اثر (athar): A narration from a companion or successor (not directly from the Prophet).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hadith: 'People of two religions do not inherit from each other'
B) The athar from Sufyan: 'Islam is one religion and shirk is one religion'
C) The Qur'anic verse on inheritance
D) The consensus of the companions

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, all non-Muslims are considered one millah for inheritance, so they inherit from each other regardless of specific faith.

Difference of Religion Bars Inheritance
Ruling with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a Muslim cannot inherit from a disbeliever and vice versa, and cite the hadith proof from Bukhari and Abu Dawud.

Core Idea
Difference of religion (Islam vs. kufr) is an absolute bar to inheritance.

This lesson establishes one of the fundamental barriers to inheritance in Islamic law: difference of religion. The author presents the ruling concisely and supports it with the famous hadith from Usama ibn Zayd, which is agreed upon by all major hadith collections. We will analyze the text, the proof, and the implications of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states that a Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever and vice versa. Note the double negation: it applies in both directions.
2
Recognize the proof
The author cites the hadith of Usama ibn Zayd. Locate the hadith: 'A Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever, nor does a disbeliever inherit from a Muslim.'
This hadith is found in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Understand the implication
The bar is absolute; no exception is made for close blood relations. The commentary emphasizes that Islam and kufr are completely separate religions.
4
Note the authority
The ruling is part of Zahir al-Riwayah and is universally agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) in the Hanafi school, though there are cross-madhhab differences on what constitutes 'difference of religion'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۲۳۲] (۴) ولايرث المسلم الكافر ولا الكافرُ المسلم

[۳۲۳۲] (۴) مسلمان کافر کا اور کافر مسلمان کا وارث نہیں ہو گا۔
او پر حدیث گزری کہ دو مذہب والے ایک دوسرے کے وارث نہیں ہو نگے ۔ یہاں تو کفر اور اسلام بالکل الگ الگ مذہب ہے اس لئے کسی حال میں وارث نہیں ہوگا (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن اسامة بن زيد ان النبي الله قال لا يرث المسلم المكافر ولا الكافر المسلم (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب لایت المسلم الکافرولا الکافر مسلم ص ۱۰۰۱ نمبر ۶۷۶۴ رابوداؤد شریف ، باب بل میرٹ المسلم الکافر ، ج ۲، ص ۴۷، نمبر ۲۹۰۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسلمان کا فر کا اور کا فرمسلمان کا وارث نہیں ہوگا۔
[3232] (4) Neither does a Muslim inherit from a disbeliever nor does a disbeliever inherit from a Muslim.

[3232] (4) A Muslim will not inherit from a disbeliever, and a disbeliever will not inherit from a Muslim.
The hadith has already passed that people of two religions do not inherit from each other. Here, disbelief and Islam are completely separate religions, therefore in no case will they inherit. (2) There is a hadith: From Usama ibn Zayd that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'A Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever, nor does a disbeliever inherit from a Muslim.' (a) (Bukhari, ...; Abu Dawud, ...). From this hadith it is known that a Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever and a disbeliever does not inherit from a Muslim.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof, establishing a clear bar to inheritance between Muslims and disbelievers. The author explicitly states that a Muslim cannot inherit from a disbeliever and vice versa. The proof is the famous hadith narrated by Usama ibn Zayd, which is found in both Bukhari and Abu Dawud. The commentary notes that this is an application of the general principle from the earlier hadith about two religions not inheriting. Since Islam and kufr are completely separate religions, the bar is absolute. This ruling is part of Zahir al-Riwayah and is universally agreed upon among the schools.

Key Terms
مخالف في الدين (mukhalif fi al-din): Difference in religion (Islam vs. kufr) that bars inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) The Muslim inherits only if the father was a Christian.
D) The disbeliever's property goes to the state.

Key Takeaway
Difference of religion between a Muslim and a disbeliever is an absolute bar to inheritance according to the explicit hadith.

Property of an Apostate: Pre- and Post-Apostasy Wealth
States ruling on apostate's property with proof from 'Ali's action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an apostate's pre- and post-apostasy property, identify the dalil from the action of 'Ali (ra), and explain why post-apostasy wealth is classified as fay'.

Core Idea
An apostate's pre-apostasy wealth is inherited by Muslim heirs; post-apostasy earnings are fay' for the public treasury.

This passage addresses a critical faraid question: what happens to the property of someone who leaves Islam? The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the time of acquisition. Let's examine the ruling, its proof from the practice of Caliph 'Ali (ra), and the reasoning behind the distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of property
The text divides the apostate's property into two categories: (1) property acquired while Muslim (before apostasy) and (2) property acquired after apostasy (while a disbeliever).
2
State the ruling for each category
For category (1), the property goes to the apostate's Muslim heirs. For category (2), the property is considered fay' (spoils) and goes to the public treasury (bayt al-mal).
3
Understand the legal reasoning
While Muslim, the apostate and his heirs share the same religion, so inheritance is valid. After apostasy, he is a disbeliever, and a Muslim cannot inherit from a disbeliever (based on the hadith 'The Muslim does not inherit from the disbeliever').
This is the same principle applied in the general rule of inheritance between Muslims and non-Muslims.
4
Examine the dalil: action of 'Ali (ra)
The author cites an athar: 'Ali executed an apostate and distributed his pre-apostasy wealth among his Muslim relatives. This demonstrates the practice of the Companions and is used as evidence.
The dalil is a qawl sahabi (saying/action of a Companion), which is considered a valid proof in Hanafi usul.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that all of the apostate's property (both pre- and post-apostasy) goes to bayt al-mal, not to Muslim heirs. The Hanafi school distinguishes based on the time of acquisition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۲۳۳] (۵) ومال المرتد لورثته المسلمين وما اكتسبه في حال رِدَّتِه فىءٌ.

(۳۲۳۳) (۵) مرتد کا مال اس کے مسلمان ورثہ کا ہوگا۔ اور جو کچھ کمایا مرتد کی حالت میں وہ غنیمت ہے۔ مرتد چونکہ کا فر ہو چکا ہے اس لئے حالت ارتداد میں جو کچھ کمایا اس کا وارث مسلمان نہیں ہو سکتا کیونکہ اوپر گزر چکا ہے کہ مسلمان کا فر کا وارث نہیں ہوسکتا۔ البتہ اسلام کی حالت میں جو کچھ کمایا اس کا وارث مسلمان ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ دونوں کا مذہب ایک ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن على انه اتى بمستورد العجلي وقد ارتد فعرض عليه الاسلام فابي فقتله وجعل ميراثة بين ورژته من المسلمين (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی هیته ۸۰۰ فی المرتد عن الاسلام، ج سادس بس ۲۸۱، نمبر ۳۱۳۷۵ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب میراث المرتد ، ج عاشر ص ۳۳۹ نمبر ۱۹۲۹۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرتد کا اسلام کے زمانے میں کمایا ہوا مال مسلمان ورثہ کے درمیان تقسیم ہو گا۔ اور کفر کے زمانے کا مال گویا کہ حربی کا مال ہوا اس لئے وہ فی شمار کیا جائے گا۔
[3233] (5) And the property of the apostate belongs to his Muslim heirs, and whatever he acquired in the state of his apostasy is fay' (spoils).

(3233) (5) The property of an apostate will go to his Muslim heirs. And whatever he earned in the state of apostasy is booty. Since the apostate has become a disbeliever, whatever he earned in the state of apostasy cannot be inherited by a Muslim, because it has already been stated that a Muslim cannot inherit from a disbeliever. However, whatever he earned in the state of Islam will be inherited by his Muslim heirs because both have the same religion. There is an athar: From 'Ali that a man named Mustawrid al-'Ijli was brought before him who had apostatized. 'Ali presented Islam to him, but he refused, so 'Ali killed him and divided his inheritance among his Muslim heirs. (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, ...; Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, ...). From this athar it is known that the wealth earned by the apostate during the time of Islam will be distributed among the Muslim heirs. And the wealth from the time of disbelief is like the property of a harbi (enemy combatant), so it will be considered fay' (spoils).
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The author distinguishes between two categories of an apostate's property: (1) property acquired before apostasy (while Muslim) goes to his Muslim heirs, because at the time of earning, both were Muslims and of the same religion. (2) Property acquired after apostasy (while a disbeliever) is considered fay' (spoils of war), because the apostate is now a disbeliever, and a Muslim cannot inherit from a disbeliever. The proof is the action of Caliph 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, who executed an apostate and distributed his pre-apostasy wealth among his Muslim relatives. The post-apostasy wealth according to the Hanafi school goes to the public treasury (bayt al-mal) as fay'. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
فىء (fay'): Spoils of war or property acquired from disbelievers without battle; here, the apostate's post-apostasy earnings are treated as fay' and go to the public treasury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the fate of property acquired by an apostate after he leaves Islam?
A) It is inherited by his Muslim heirs.
B) It becomes fay' and goes to the public treasury.
C) It is given to his non-Muslim relatives.
D) It is destroyed.

Key Takeaway
An apostate's wealth is split by time: pre-apostasy goes to Muslim heirs, post-apostasy is fay' for the public treasury.

Simultaneous Death: No Inheritance Between Unknown-Order Victims
States the ruling on inheritance when order of death is unknown (gharq/hadd) with athar proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inheritance when the order of death is unknown and apply it to a simultaneous death scenario.

Core Idea
When order of death is unknown, simultaneous victims do not inherit from each other — each estate passes to their living heirs.

In inheritance cases where multiple heirs die in a common accident and the sequence of death cannot be determined, a special rule applies. This lesson explains the Hanafi position based on the practice of Caliph 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, which prevents circular inheritance and ensures clarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The ruling applies when a group dies together (e.g., drowning, building collapse) and the order of death is unknown.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the text, each deceased person's property goes to their living heirs, not to the other deceased co-victims.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the practice of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, who would give inheritance to the living from the dead and not make the drowned inherit from each other.
Recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and al-Darimi.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Caliph's practice directly demonstrates the ruling: when order is unknown, no inheritance passes between the co-victims. The word 'la yurith' (does not make inherit) indicates prohibition.
The thubut is zanni but dalala is qati.
5
Apply the ruling to a case
Consider a father and son drowning together, each survived by other relatives. Neither inherits from the other; the father's estate goes to his other living heirs, the son's to his.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۲۳۴] (۲) واذا غرق جماعة او سقطت عليهم حائط فلم يُعلم من مات منهم اولا فمال كل واحد منهم للاحياء من ورثته.

[۳۲۳۴] (۶) اگر ایک جماعت ڈوب گئی یا ان پر دیوار گر گئی اور معلوم نہیں ہوا کہ ان میں سے کون پہلے مرا تو ان میں سے ہر ایک کا مال اس کے زندہ ورثہ کے لئے ہوگا۔
ایک جماعت کے لوگ آپس میں رشتہ دار تھے اور ایک دوسرے کے وارث تھے ۔ سبھی کشتی میں ڈوب کر مر گئے ۔ یہ معلوم نہیں ہوا کہ کون پہلے مرا اور کون بعد میں تو ایسی صورت میں وہ لوگ آپس میں وارث نہیں ہوں گے۔ بلکہ جو لوگ زندہ ہیں وہ لوگ وارث ہوں گے۔ عن عمر بن عبد العزيز انه كان يورث الاحياء من الاموات ولا يورث الغرقى بعضهم من بعض (ج) مصنف ابن ابی شبيبة ، ۴۷م من قال سرت كل واحد منهم وارثه من الناس ولا يورث بعضهم من بعض، ج سادس ،ص ۲۷۸ نمبر ۳۱۳۴۰ رالدارمی ، باب میراث الغرقی ، ج ثانی ص ۴۷۳، نمبر ۳۰۴۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ غرق ہونے والے ایک دوسرے کے مالک نہیں ہوں گے بلکہ ان کے بعد جو زندہ ہیں وہ وارث ہوں گے۔
[3234] (2) And if a group drowns or a wall falls upon them and it is not known who among them died first, then the property of each one of them belongs to the living among their heirs.

[3234] (6) If a group of people drown or a wall falls on them, and it is not known who died first, then the property of each of them will go to his living heirs.
A group of people were relatives and they were heirs of each other. All drowned in a boat. It is not known who died first and who later. In such a case, they will not inherit from each other. Rather, those who are alive will inherit. From 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz that he would give inheritance to the living from the dead, and would not make the drowned inherit from each other. (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, ...; al-Darimi, ...). From this athar it is known that the drowned do not become owners of each other's property; rather, those who are alive after them are the heirs.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. When a group of potential heirs die in a common disaster (drowning, building collapse) and the order of death cannot be ascertained, Hanafi law (based on the practice of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz) holds that none of them inherit from each other. Instead, each deceased person's estate passes to his own living heirs who did not die in the accident. This avoids the circular problem of trying to determine who died first. Thus, if a father and son both drown, the father's estate goes to the son's living relatives (e.g., the son's children) and the son's estate to the father's living relatives (e.g., the father's parents), but not to each other. This ruling is part of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
الغرقى (al-gharqa): People who die together in a drowning or similar disaster where order of death is unknown.
يورث الاحياء من الاموات (yurith al-ahya' min al-amwat): The practice of giving inheritance to the living from the dead, i.e., the living heirs inherit from the deceased, but not the co-deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a father and son both drown in a shipwreck and it is unknown who died first, how is inheritance determined?
A) The father inherits from the son.
B) The son inherits from the father.
C) Neither inherits from the other; each estate goes to their own living heirs.
D) The state takes all property.

Key Takeaway
When order of death is unknown among simultaneous deaths, Hanafi law prevents inheritance between them; each estate passes to the living heirs.

Majusi Inheritance: One Relationship Only
Ruling on Majusi inheriting through only one of two possible familial relationships.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a Majusi inherits through only one of two conflicting relationships and identify whether that relationship is determined by halal or closeness.

Core Idea
A Zoroastrian inherits only through one relationship, not both, even if two arise from their invalid marriage.

This lesson explores a unique faraid issue: when a Zoroastrian (Majusi) has two familial ties to the same person due to a consanguineous marriage (e.g., a woman is both mother and wife). Islamic law does not recognize both as valid for inheritance. We will learn the Hanafi rule that only one inheritance passes, based on either the halal relationship or the nearer lineage, supported by athar from early authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting relationships
In a Majusi family, a person may be related to the deceased through two different relations (e.g., mother and wife, or daughter and half-sister). List those relationships.
These arise from the Majusi practice of marrying close relatives, which is invalid in Islam.
2
Determine which relationship is halal
Check if one of the relationships is naturally valid in Islamic law (e.g., motherhood is always halal, marriage to mother is not). The halal relationship takes precedence.
If both are from invalid marriages, move to step 3.
3
Apply the 'nearer lineage' rule
If both relationships are equally invalid, choose the one that is closer in blood or the one with the stronger claim according to the athar 'he inherits through the nearer of the two lineages.'
This is based on the report from al-Zuhri.
4
Distribute inheritance through one relationship
The heir receives the share corresponding to the chosen relationship, not a sum of both shares. For example, as mother (1/6) but not also as wife.
The judge must decide which single relationship applies.

(7) And if two relationships come together in a Majusi, such that if they were separated in two persons, each would inherit from the other along with others, then the Majusi inherits through one of them. (8) And the Majusi does not inherit through the invalid marriages that they consider permissible. A Majusi considers it permissible to marry his mother and daughter. For example, he married his mother: she becomes both mother and wife. When this Majusi dies, should this woman inherit as mother or as wife or both? The author says: the relationship which is halal will give inheritance. So she will inherit as mother, not as wife. Another example: from this woman a daughter is born to the Majusi. This daughter is also a daughter and also a half-sister (maternal) because she is the daughter of the Majusi's mother. Which inheritance should she get? As daughter or as half-sister or both? The author says that here both being a daughter and being a half-sister are due to a forbidden marriage, so give her inheritance through one relationship, not both. Because according to Islamic Shari'ah, such two relationships cannot exist; only one relationship is possible. So give inheritance through one relationship. (2) In the athar: from al-Zuhri, he said: 'He inherits through the nearer of the two lineages.' (Another narration: I asked Hammad about the inheritance of the Majusi; he said: 'They inherit from the side that is halal.') (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 31412/31416) In this athar, it is said that from the two relationships, the one that is closer will be the basis for inheritance. And in the other narration, the relationship that is halal will be the basis.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage deals with inheritance for Magians (Zoroastrians) who practice consanguineous marriages (e.g., mother-daughter) that are invalid in Islam but permissible in their religion. The ruling is that a Majusi will inherit through only one of the two relationships that arise from such a marriage, not both. The principle is to choose the relationship that is halal (valid) in Islamic law or, if both are invalid, the closest one. The author provides examples: a man marries his mother, so she is both mother and wife; she inherits as mother because that relationship is halal (motherhood is valid), not as wife (since marriage to mother is invalid). If a daughter is born, she is both daughter and half-sister; both relationships come from a forbidden marriage, so she inherits through only one (the closer one, or whichever is considered). Evidence is cited from al-Zuhri (inherits through near lineage) and Hammad (inherits through halal side). This illustrates how Islamic law accommodates the existing family structures of non-Muslims while rejecting their invalid relationships.

Key Terms
مجوسي (majusi): A Zoroastrian, considered a People of the Book with their own marriage customs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because both relationships (daughter and half-sister) come from an invalid marriage.
C) Because she has a choice.
D) Because the father was not Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A Majusi inherits through only one of two conflicting relationships arising from an invalid marriage, chosen by either the halal side or the nearer lineage.

Magian Inheritance Through Invalid Marriages
Ruling with dalil from Hammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on inheritance through invalid marriages for Magians and apply the condition that only halal relationships are recognized in inheritance.

Core Idea
Inheritance rights for Magians are based on Islamic law, not their own—invalid marriages yield no inheritance.

This passage addresses a specific case: the inheritance rights of Magians who practice incestuous marriages (e.g., marrying a sister) considered valid in their religion. Islamic law does not recognize such marriages as valid, and therefore no inheritance rights arise from them. The ruling rests on the principle that inheritance relationships are determined by Islamic criteria, regardless of the parties' own beliefs. The author cites an athar from Hammad to reinforce this point.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Magians may consider marriages to close relatives (mother, daughter, sister) as permissible. Understand that our law does not accept these as valid marriages.
2
State the ruling
The text states: 'The Majusi does not inherit through the invalid marriages that they consider permissible.' That is, no inheritance through such relationships.
3
Examine the dalil
The author cites the athar: 'I asked Hammad about the inheritance of the Majusi; he said: They inherit from the side that is halal.' This restricts inheritance to relationships that are Islamically valid.
4
Apply the principle
From the athar, extract the rule: only halal relationships (e.g., proper marriage, valid blood ties) create inheritance. Invalid marriages are disregarded.
If a woman is both a wife through an invalid marriage and a sister through blood, she inherits only as a sister, not as a wife.
5
Work through an example
Suppose a Magian man dies who married his sister. She does not inherit as a wife, but she may inherit as a sister if there are no closer heirs. A woman married properly would inherit as a wife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

حافظ : دیوار

(8) And the Majusi does not inherit through the invalid marriages that they consider permissible in their religion. A Majusi will not inherit through a marriage that he considers permissible in his religion but is invalid in Islam. They consider it permissible to marry their mothers, daughters, sisters. But in Shari'ah, marriage to such mahram relatives is haram. Therefore, they will not inherit through such marriages. Rather, they will inherit through marriage to halal women. The athar has passed: 'I asked Hammad about the inheritance of the Majusi; he said: They inherit from the side that is halal.'
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This passage emphatically restates that inheritance relationships for Magians are determined by Islamic law, not by their own religion. If a marriage is invalid in Islam (e.g., marriage to a mahram), then any relationship arising from it does not grant inheritance rights. The author uses the same athar from Hammad: 'They inherit from the side that is halal.' This means that while Magians may practice such marriages, for inheritance purposes, only those relationships that are halal in Islam are recognized. Therefore, a woman married through incestuous marriage does not inherit as a wife, nor does a child born from such a marriage inherit through both relationships; only one relationship (the closest or halal) may be considered, as per the previous ruling.

Key Terms
نكاح فاسد (nikah fāsid): A marriage that is invalid in Islamic law, though the parties may consider it valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Magians inherit only through relationships that are halal in Islam; invalid marriages do not create inheritance rights.

Magian Inheritance with Two Relationships
Ruling on Magian with two relationships

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for a Magian who has two family relationships that would each allow inheritance, and apply the principle of inheritance through the permissible relationship.

Core Idea
A Magian inherits only through the valid relationship, not through an invalid marriage.

This lesson addresses a specific inheritance rule for Magians, who may have conflicting relationships due to invalid marriages. The Hanafi school, based on early Muslim authorities, rules that the Magian inherits only through the relationship that is permissible in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The case involves a Magian who has two family relationships that, if they were in separate persons, would allow one to inherit from the other.
E.g., a woman who is both mother and wife due to an invalid marriage.
2
State the Rule
The Magian inherits through only one of these relationships, not both.
3
Determine the Valid Relationship
Based on the athar from al-Zuhri and Hammad, the valid relationship is the nearer lineage or the one that is permissible in Islamic law.
Permissible means a relationship that is recognized in Islam, such as motherhood, not an incestuous marriage.
4
Apply to the Mother-Wife Example
She inherits as a mother because that relationship is valid; the wife relationship is invalid.
5
Identify the Evidence
The ruling is based on the athar: 'He inherits through the nearer of the two lines' and 'through the face that is permissible.'
The evidence is a qawl sahabi (statement of a companion) with zanni transmission and meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اجتمع فى المجوسی قرابتان لوتفرقت فى شخصين ورث احدهما مع الأخر وُرّث بهما
And if in a Magian two relationships come together that would, if separated in two persons, one would inherit from the other, then he is made to inherit through one of them.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This is a ruling from the chapter on inheritance of Magians. Magians consider it permissible to marry their mothers and daughters. If a Magian marries his mother, she becomes both mother and wife. Upon his death, the author states that she inherits only through the relationship that is valid in Islamic law—motherhood—not through the invalid marriage. Similarly, if a daughter is born from that marriage, she has two relationships: daughter (via invalid marriage) and maternal half-sister (also via invalid marriage). Since both relationships arise from an invalid marriage, she only inherits through one of them, based on the athar from al-Zuhri that she inherits through the nearer of the two lines of descent, and from Hammad that she inherits through the line that is permissible.

Key Terms
مجوسی (majūsī): A follower of the Magian religion who is treated as a non-Muslim with his own inheritance rules.
قرابتان (qarābatān): Two familial relationships that would normally be separate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Magians and Invalid Marriages: No Inheritance Rights
Ruling that Magians do not inherit through forbidden marriages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that inheritance requires a valid marriage and apply it to scenarios involving invalid marriages.

Core Idea
Inheritance follows valid lineage, not permissibility in one's religion.

This passage addresses a specific case: Magians (Zoroastrians) practice marriages that are prohibited in Islam, such as between close relatives. The Hanafi school rules that such marriages do not create inheritance rights, even if they are culturally or religiously accepted. Only relationships that are valid in Islamic law—through permissible marriages—confer inheritance. This reinforces the principle that Islamic inheritance is based on recognized legal relationships, not custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the inheritance by a Magian from a relative through a marriage that is invalid in Islamic law. The ruling is that such inheritance does not occur.
2
Understand the condition for inheritance
Inheritance depends on a valid legal relationship. A marriage that is fasid (invalid) does not create the bond of spousal inheritance.
The marriage itself is considered nonexistent for inheritance purposes.
3
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a Magian who marries his sister. Upon his death, his sister does not inherit as a wife, because the marriage is invalid. She may still inherit as a sister if she is a blood relative, but not through the marriage.
The ruling does not affect blood relations that are valid in Islam.
4
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
Some other schools might recognize inheritance through blood relations even if the marriage is invalid, but the Hanafi school strictly restricts inheritance to relationships that are permissible in Islamic law.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولايرث المجوسى بالانكحة الفاسدة التي يستحلونها في دينهم
And the Magian does not inherit through invalid marriages that they consider permissible in their religion.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This is a clear ruling from the same chapter. Magians consider it permissible to marry mahram relatives such as mothers, daughters, and sisters. However, in Islamic law, these marriages are invalid. Therefore, a Magian does not inherit from such spouses or through such relationships. He only inherits from those with whom he has a valid relationship in Islamic law, i.e., through permissible marriages. The commentary cites the same athar from Hammad: 'They inherit from the line that is permissible.'

Key Terms
انكحة فاسدة (ankiha fāsida): Marriages that are invalid in Islamic law, such as those between mahram relatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Magian man marries his sister (a marriage they consider permissible). He dies. Does she inherit from him?
A) Yes, because she is his sister.
B) Yes, because they consider it permissible.
C) No, because the marriage is invalid in Islamic law.
D) No, because sisters never inherit.

Key Takeaway
A marriage that is invalid in Islamic law does not create inheritance rights, even if the couple considers it permissible in their own religion.

Asabah of Child of Zina and Li'an
Ruling on asabah of zina and li'an child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the asabah of a child born from zina or li'an and identify the hadith evidence that establishes this ruling.

Core Idea
The child of zina or li'an inherits only through the mother; her male relatives become the asabah.

This lesson addresses a unique rule in Hanafi inheritance: a child born from unlawful intercourse (zina) or a child of li'an (mutual imprecation) has no legal father. Consequently, the child's inheritance network is limited to the maternal side. The mother's male relatives become the agnatic heirs (asabah). We will examine the primary texts that establish this ruling, including hadith from the Prophet ﷺ.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the legal rule: the asabah of a child of zina or li'an are the mother's relatives (mawla ummihima).
The term 'mawla' here refers to the mother's kinship group, not a freed slave.
2
Define key terms
Understand the definitions of walad al-zina, walad al-mula'ana, and asaba in the Hanafi context.
For li'an, the father denies paternity through a formal process; after li'an, the child is attributed solely to the mother.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
Examine the three hadith cited: (1) Mak'hul: the Prophet gave inheritance of the child of li'an to the mother and her heirs. (2) Ibn Umar: the Prophet separated the couple and attributed the child to the woman. (3) Amr ibn Shu'ayb: the Prophet decreed that a child from zina does not inherit nor give inheritance.
These hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted as evidence in Hanafi school.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a child born from zina who dies leaving a mother, maternal uncle, and biological father. Determine the asabah.
The maternal uncle is the asaba; the biological father inherits nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعصبة ولد الزنا وولد الملاعنة مولى امهما
And the asabah of the child of zina and the child of li'an is the master (i.e., relatives) of their mother.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This ruling states that the agnatic heirs ('asabah) for a child born from zina (adultery) or a child of li'an (mutual imprecation) are the mother's relatives. Since the father is not legally recognized, the child is attributed to the mother. Therefore, inheritance goes to the mother's side. The commentary provides hadith evidence: for li'an, the Prophet ﷺ gave the inheritance to the mother and her heirs; for zina, the Prophet ﷺ said such a child does not inherit from nor give inheritance to the father. Thus, the mother's relatives become the 'asabah.

Key Terms
ولد الزنا (walad al-zinā): A child born from unlawful sexual intercourse (zina).
ولد الملاعنة (walad al-mulāʿana): A child whose father denies paternity through li'an (mutual imprecation) after accusing the mother of adultery.
عصبة (asaba): Agnatic heirs who inherit by residuary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A child born from zina dies. Who are his 'asabah?
A) His biological father's relatives.
B) His mother's relatives.
C) The state (public treasury).
D) He has no 'asabah.

Key Takeaway
The asabah of a child of zina or li'an are exclusively the mother's relatives, as established by ahad hadith.

Deferring Inheritance for an Unborn Child
Ruling on suspending estate distribution when a widow is pregnant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on suspending estate distribution when a pregnant widow survives, and apply it to a simple faraid scenario.

Core Idea
A fetus's share is unknown, so the estate must wait until birth to distribute correctly.

This brief passage from al-Sharh al-Thamirī presents a key faraid rule: when a deceased man leaves a pregnant wife, the estate is not divided until the child is born. This ensures that the child's inheritance share—which depends on gender and number—is correctly allocated. Imam Abu Hanifa's view is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the distribution of the estate upon death. The ruling is that it is suspended (waqf) until the wife delivers.
The ruling is specific to cases where the widow is pregnant at the time of death.
2
Understand the reason behind the suspension
The fetus's share is unknown: a son receives twice the share of a daughter. Distributing prematurely could lead to incorrect shares.
This is based on the need for certainty in inheritance (yaqīn).
3
Locate the implicit proof
The implicit proof is the Quranic inheritance verses (e.g., Surah al-Nisa) that mandate specific shares. The principle of certainty requires knowing the exact number of heirs before distribution.
No explicit dalil is cited, but it is derived from the general rules of faraid.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text says 'fi qawl Abi Hanifa', implying that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani may have allowed distribution with a guarantee or condition.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's view of suspension.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
For example: A man dies leaving a pregnant wife and two adult sons. The estate is suspended until birth. After birth, if the child is a boy, shares are recalculated (wife: 1/8, sons: residue, new son: shares accordingly).
This prevents errors that would necessitate redistribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن مات وترك حملا وقف ماله حتى تضع امرأته حملها في قول ابي حنيفة رحمه الله
And whoever dies and leaves a pregnancy, his wealth is suspended until his wife delivers her pregnancy, according to the saying of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This is a ruling from the same chapter. If a deceased man leaves a pregnant wife, the distribution of his estate is postponed until the child is born. This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentary explains that if the pregnancy is the only child, the entire estate waits. If there are other children, the share for the pregnancy is set aside—if a boy is born, he gets more; if a girl, less. The distribution is delayed to avoid errors.

Key Terms
حمل (ḥaml): A fetus in the womb.
وقف (waqf): To suspend, defer; here, the estate is not distributed until delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man dies, leaving a pregnant wife and two adult sons. What happens to the estate according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Distributed immediately among the sons and wife.
B) Suspended until the child is born, then re-divided.
C) The child's share is ignored.
D) The wife gets nothing until she delivers.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, the estate of a deceased with a pregnant wife is suspended until the child is born to ensure correct allocation of shares.

Inheritance of Children of Zina and Li'an: Mother's Relatives as 'Asabah
Ruling and proof on 'asabah for children of zina and li'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who serves as 'asabah for children born from zina or li'an and identify the hadith proofs that establish this ruling.

Core Idea
Children of zina and li'an have no father; their 'asabah are the mother's relatives.

In Hanafi faraid, the 'asabah (male agnate heirs) are typically the paternal relatives. However, for children born from zina (adultery) or li'an (the oath of condemnation that severs paternity), the child has no recognized father. This lesson examines the ruling that the mother's relatives step in as the 'asabah, based on explicit hadith evidence. Understanding this exception is crucial for correct inheritance distribution in these sensitive cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The ruling concerns the 'asabah for two categories of children: those born from zina (no legal father) and those born from li'an (paternity severed). The ruling states that the mother's relatives are the 'asabah.
This is a faraid ruling, not an act of worship.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites three hadith: one from Abu Dawud on the child of li'an inheriting from the mother and her heirs, one from Bukhari showing the Prophet attributed the child to the mother, and one from Tirmidhi stating the child of zina does not inherit from the father nor cause inheritance.
These are ahadith, but their meaning is clear (qat'i al-dalala).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly establish that paternal inheritance is completely cut off for these children, leaving the mother as the sole link. The phrase 'lā yarithu wa lā yūrath' (does not inherit nor cause inheritance) in the Tirmidhi hadith confirms that the father's side has no rights.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
While the Hanafi school adheres firmly to this ruling, other schools may have differing views, for example allowing some inheritance from the father's side under certain conditions. Understanding this difference is important for comparative fiqh.
The Hanafi position is based on the apparent meaning of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دينهم ۱۳۳۷ (۹) وعصبة ولد الزنا وولد الملاعنة مولى امهما زنا سے جو بچہ پیدا ہوا ہے شرعی اعتبار سے اس کا باپ نہیں ہے۔ یا جس عورت سے باپ نے لعان کر لیا تو اس بچے کا رشتہ باپ سے ختم ہو گیا۔ اب وہ باپ ہی نہیں رہا۔ اس لئے نہ باپ وارث ہو گا اور نہ باپ کے رشتہ دار وارث ہوں گے ۔ بلکہ اس کا تعلق ماں کے ساتھ ہو گیا۔ اس لئے ماں وارث ہوگی اور ماں کے رشتہ دار وارث ہوں گے۔ اور یہ لڑکا ماں کا وارث ہوگا اور ماں کی جانب سے جو رشتہ دار ہیں ان کا وارث ہوگا۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ حدثنا مكحول قال جعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم میراث ابن الملاعنة لامه ولورثتها من بعدها (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب میراث ابن الملاعہ یہ بھی ۲۷ نمبر ۲۹۰۷) (۲) بخاری میں اس طرح ہے۔ عن ابن عمر ان رجلا لا عن امرأته في زمن النبي الا الله و انتفى من ولدها ففرق النبى الله الله بينهما والحق الولد بالمرأة (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب میراث الملاعیہ ، ص ۹۹۹، نمبر ۶۷۴۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جس عورت سے لعان کیا اس عورت کا وہ بچہ باپ کا وارث نہیں ہوگا۔ اور نہ باپ اس کا وارث ہوگا۔ بلکہ عورت بچے کا وارث ہوگی اور بچہ ماں کا وارث ہوگا۔ اور زنا سے پیدا شدہ بچے کے بارے میں یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عمر بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ايما رجل عاهر بحرة او امة فالولد ولد زنا لا يرث ولا يورث (ج) ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی ابطال میراث ولد الزنا ص ۳۱ نمبر ۲۱۱۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ باپ کو نہ لڑکے کی وراثت ملے گی اور نہ لڑ کا باپ کا وارث ہو گا۔ ملاعیہ : وہ عورت جس نے زنا کی تہمت کی وجہ سے شوہر سے لعان کیا، مولی : آقا ، یہاں ماں کے رشتہ دار مراد ہیں۔
Their religion [marginal] (9) And the 'asabah of the child of zina and the child of li'an are the relatives of their mother. A child born from zina, according to Islamic law, does not have a father. Or a woman with whom the father performed li'an, the child's relation to the father is severed. Now the father does not exist. Therefore, neither the father inherits nor the father's relatives inherit. Rather, the child's connection is with the mother. So the mother inherits and the mother's relatives inherit. And this boy inherits from the mother and inherits from the relatives on the mother's side. There is proof of this in hadith: Makhul narrated: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) made the inheritance of the son of li'an for his mother and her heirs after her. (a) (Abu Dawud, Book of Inheritance of Li'an, hadith 2907) (2) In Bukhari it is: Ibn 'Umar narrated that a man performed li'an with his wife during the Prophet's time and disowned her child. The Prophet separated them and attributed the child to the woman. (b) (Bukhari, Book of Inheritance of Li'an, p. 999, hadith 6748) From this hadith, it is understood that the child of the woman with whom li'an was performed does not inherit from the father, nor does the father inherit from him. Rather, the woman inherits from the child and the child inherits from the mother. And regarding a child born from zina, there is this hadith: 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Messenger of Allah said: Any man who commits adultery with a free woman or a slave girl, the child is a child of zina; he does not inherit nor does he cause inheritance. (c) (Tirmidhi, Book of Abolishing Inheritance of Child of Zina, p. 31, hadith 2113) In this hadith, the father does not receive inheritance from the boy, nor does the boy inherit from the father. Li'an: the woman who performed li'an with her husband due to accusation of zina. Mawla: master; here meaning the mother's relatives.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from a matn along with its proof and commentary. The ruling states that for children born from zina (adultery) or from li'an (the oath of condemnation between spouses), the 'asabah (male agnate relatives) are the relatives from the mother's side. The reason is that such children have no legal father according to Shariah. In the case of zina, the biological father is not considered a legal father, so he and his relatives do not inherit. In li'an, the father disowns the child through the process of li'an, severing the paternal lineage. Thus, the child's inheritance ties are only with the mother and her relatives. The author provides three hadith as proof: (1) The Prophet assigned the inheritance of the child of li'an to the mother and her heirs. (2) A report that the Prophet attributed the child to the woman after li'an. (3) A hadith stating that a child of zina does not inherit from the father, nor does the father inherit from him. The commentary also explains the terms 'li'an' (the woman who performed li'an) and 'mawla' (here meaning relatives of the mother). This ruling is well-established in the Hanafi school and is based on clear Sunnah.

Key Terms
ولد الزنا (walad al-zina): A child born from fornication (zina); has no legal father in Shariah.
ولد الملاعنة (walad al-mula'anah): A child born from a woman who performed li'an (mutual cursing) with her husband, disowning the child; the child's paternal lineage is severed.
عصبة (asabah): Male agnate relatives who inherit the residue after prescribed shares are given.
مولی (mawla): Here means the mother's relatives (as 'asabah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The father's relatives
B) The mother's relatives
C) The child has no 'asabah
D) The state

Key Takeaway
For children of zina and li'an, the mother's relatives serve as the 'asabah; the father's lineage is entirely severed.
