Base Number for Fourth and Remainder or Half
Defining the base number (asl) for faraid cases involving fourth and remainder or half

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the base number (asl al-mas'alah) for faraid cases where the only prescribed shares are one-fourth and remainder, or one-fourth and one-half.

Core Idea
When shares are limited to fourth and remainder, or fourth and half, the base number is always 4.

In inheritance calculations, the base number (asl) is the denominator from which all shares are derived. This lesson covers a specific rule: when the estate includes a 1/4 share (e.g., wife or husband when there is a child) and the rest goes to an asabah (residuary), or when there is both 1/4 and 1/2, the base is simply 4. This makes distribution straightforward, as the shares are already compatible with a denominator of 4.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prescribed shares
List all fard (Quranic) shares in the case. Look for a 1/4 share (e.g., wife, husband with child) and note if the remaining shares are only half (1/2) or residue (asabah).
If there are shares other than 1/4, 1/2, or residue, this rule does not apply.
2
Check for compatibility with base 4
Verify that the prescribed fractions are 1/4, 1/2, or remainder (expressed as fraction of 4). Since 1/2 = 2/4 and remainder can be 3/4 or 1/4, all denominators are 4.
If there is a 1/8 share, the base would be 8, not 4.
3
Set the base number to 4
The least common multiple (LCM) of the denominators (4) is 4. Thus, the base number (asl) is 4.
This matches the LCM of 4 and 2 (for half), which is 4.
4
Distribute shares using base 4
Assign each heir their fractional share as a portion of 4. For example, a wife entitled to 1/4 gets 1 out of 4, and the residuary gets the remaining 3.
If there is a half share (2/4) and a fourth (1/4), the residuary gets the remaining 1/4.

3255 (3) If there is a fourth and remainder, or a fourth and half, its base is from four. The problem will be formed thus: Deceased 3, two daughters (2), uncle (1) [calculator calculation: 100, two daughters 66.66, uncle 33.33]. In this problem, two daughters are given two-thirds, i.e., 66.66 out of 100 as shares, and the remaining one-third, i.e., 33.33, is given to the uncle as asabah. 32551 (3) And if there is a fourth and remainder, or fourth and half, then the base is from four. For example, if a wife and grandfather are left, the wife gets one-fourth and the grandfather gets the remaining three-fourths as asabah. Therefore the base is four. The problem will be thus: Deceased 4, wife 1, grandfather 3. Calculator calculation: 100, wife 25, grandfather 75. In this problem, the wife is given one-fourth, i.e., 25 out of 100, and the remaining three-fourths, i.e., 75, is given to the grandfather as asabah. The case of fourth and half is: A woman left behind a husband, one daughter, and an uncle. Since there is one daughter, she gets half. Because of the child, the husband gets one-fourth. And the remaining one-fourth is given to the uncle as asabah. The base is four. The problem will be thus: Deceased 4, husband 1, daughter 2, uncle 1. Calculator calculation: 100, husband 25, daughter 50, uncle 25. In this problem, one-fourth, i.e., 25, is given to the husband, half, i.e., 50, to the daughter, and the remaining one-fourth, i.e., 25, to the uncle.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi faraid manual, explaining how to determine the base number (asl al-mas'alah) when the estate includes a share of one-fourth (rub') and the rest as residuary, or one-fourth and one-half (nisf). The author states that in such cases, the base is 4. He then illustrates with three examples: (1) a wife and grandfather: wife takes 1/4, grandfather takes the remaining 3/4 as asabah; base 4. (2) a husband, one daughter, and an uncle: husband 1/4, daughter 1/2, uncle 1/4 as asabah; base 4. The first example in the text (two daughters and uncle) appears to be a misplacement but is included in the passage. The calculator calculations demonstrate the same distribution using percentages (100 as total). The key principle is that when the prescribed shares are limited to fourth and remainder or fourth and half, the denominators are compatible (4) and no recomposition is needed.

Key Terms
عصبہ (asabah): A male agnatic heir who takes the residue of the estate after the Quranic shares are distributed.
سہام (siham): Shares or portions of the inheritance allotted to each heir.
اصل مسئلہ (asl al-mas'alah): The base number from which the inheritance shares are derived, often the least common multiple of the denominators of the prescribed shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 2
B) 4
C) 8
D) 3

Key Takeaway
The base number is 4 whenever the only prescribed fractional shares are one-fourth and one-half.

Base Number for Eighth and Remainder or Half
Defining the base number (asl) for faraid cases involving eighth and remainder or eighth and half

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the base number (asl al-mas'alah) as 8 for faraid cases involving an eighth and a remainder, or an eighth and a half, and distribute shares accordingly.

Core Idea
When an eighth appears with any other fraction, the base must be 8 to give whole-number shares to all heirs.

In Hanafi faraid, the base number (asl al-mas'alah) is the smallest whole number from which the shares of all heirs can be derived as integers. This lesson focuses on cases where the estate includes a Quranic one-eighth (thumn) and either the remainder as residuary or a half. Both situations require a base of 8, as demonstrated by the examples of a wife and son, and a wife, daughter, and uncle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fractional shares
List all Quranic shares present. Look for an eighth (1/8) and note whether the remaining heirs take the residue (asabah) or another fixed share like a half (1/2).
In the first example: wife gets 1/8, son takes residue. In the second: wife 1/8, daughter 1/2, uncle residue.
2
Express all fractions with a common denominator
Find a common denominator that can represent each share as an integer numerator. For 1/8 and 1/2, the least common denominator is 8 (since 1/2 = 4/8).
If only 1/8 and residue, the residue is expressed as 7/8; the denominator 8 works.
3
Set the base number (asl) to that denominator
The base number is the denominator that makes all share numerators whole numbers. Here it is 8.
Base 8 for both examples.
4
Distribute the shares as integer parts of the base
Assign numerators: e.g., wife = 1, son = 7; or wife = 1, daughter = 4, uncle = 3. Sum the numerators to confirm they equal the base.
Second example: 1+4+3=8.
5
Convert to percentages or fractional values (optional)
To verify, multiply each share by 100/base. For base 8, wife = 12.5%, etc.
The text shows calculator values for clarity.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi faraid manual, explaining the base number when the estate includes an eighth (thumn) and either the remainder as residuary or a half. The author states that the base is 8. He provides two examples: (1) wife and son: wife gets 1/8, son gets the remaining 7/8 as asabah; base 8. (2) wife, one daughter, and an uncle: wife 1/8 (due to child's presence), daughter 1/2, uncle 3/8 as asabah; base 8. The calculator calculations show the same shares as percentages. The rule rests on the denominator 8, which encompasses both the eighth and the half (4/8). When both fractions appear, the base must be 8 to provide whole-number shares.

Key Terms
ثمن (thumn): One-eighth, a Quranic share assigned to the wife when there is a child, and to the husband when there is a child.
آٹھواں (aathwaan): Urdu for one-eighth, same as thumn.
اصل المسألة (asl al-mas'alah): The base number from which all heirs' shares are derived as whole integers.

Inheritance Cases with the One-Eighth Share (Thumn)
Explaining inheritance calculations with 1/8 share and remainder or 1/8 and 1/2

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the shares when a wife inherits 1/8 along with a son or with a daughter and a paternal uncle, using base number 8.

Core Idea
When the wife's share is 1/8, the base number is 8; distribute fixed shares then residue to asabah.

In faraid, the wife's share drops to 1/8 when there is a child. This lesson shows the standard method: set base 8, assign the wife 1 part, then give the remainder to the nearest male residuary. Two classic examples illustrate this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and recognize the wife's 1/8 share
Check if there is a child (son or daughter) of the deceased. If yes, the wife gets 1/8 instead of 1/4.
The presence of a child is the key condition for reducing the wife's share.
2
Set the base number (asl al-mas'alah) to 8
When 1/8 appears, the least common multiple of denominators (8) is 8. This becomes the base number.
Never use a different base like 24 unless other fractions require it.
3
Assign the wife's fixed share (fard)
The wife gets 1 part out of 8 (i.e., 1/8 of the estate).
Write it as 1/8 or 1 part.
4
Identify the residuary heir (asabah)
The residuary is the closest male relative through the father's line. In the first example it is the son; in the second it is the paternal uncle (because no son, but daughter is not residuary).
A daughter is a fixed-share heir, not a residuary, unless there are also sons.
5
Give the remaining parts to the residuary
Subtract the total fixed shares from the base. In case 1, after wife's 1 part, 7 parts remain for son. In case 2, after wife's 1 part and daughter's 4 parts (1/2 = 4/8), 3 parts remain for uncle.
Always check that fixed shares do not exceed 8; if they do, use 'awl (increase of base).

Applying 'Awl When Shares Exceed the Base: Husband and Two Full Sisters
Explaining inheritance calculations with 1/6, 1/2, and 1/3 shares and the concept of 'awl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate inheritance distributions involving 'awl, starting from identifying heirs' Quranic shares to adjusting the base number proportionally.

Core Idea
When fixed shares exceed the whole, the base number increases proportionally—this is 'awl.

Faraid calculations sometimes face a situation where the prescribed shares add up to more than the total estate. In such cases, the Hanafi school applies 'awl, increasing the base number and proportionally reducing each share. This lesson walks through a classic example: a husband and two full sisters, where shares of 1/2 and 2/3 exceed the whole.

Guided Path
1
List the heirs and their Quranic shares
Identify all surviving heirs and note their preset shares from the Quran. Here: husband (1/2) and two full sisters (2/3).
No child exists, so husband gets half.
2
Determine the base number (asl al-mas'alah)
Find the least common multiple (LCM) of the share denominators. Denominators: 2 and 3, so base = 6.
3
Observe that share total exceeds the base
Convert shares to sixths: husband = 3/6, sisters = 4/6. Total = 7/6 > 1. This triggers 'awl.
The sum of numerators exceeds the denominator.
4
Apply 'awl and recalculate shares
Increase the base number from 6 to 7. The new shares are husband = 3/7, sisters = 4/7 of the estate.
Each share is reduced proportionally, but the ratios remain the same.

[3257] (5) And if there is in it one-sixth and remainder, or half and one-third, or half and one-sixth, then its base is from six. In the problem, if there is one-sixth and remainder, or half and one-third, or half and one-sixth, then the base of the problem will be six. It will increase (awl) to seven, eight, nine, and ten. If the recipients take one-sixth share and remainder, then the problem runs from six. Sometimes the recipients will be within six shares. But sometimes the recipients will be such that if their shares are added, they will exceed six. Now the problem is made from six and the shares become seven, then the shares exceeding the base are called 'awl. The lexical meaning of 'awl is to incline and to oppress. Since the other shareholders will now suffer loss, therefore such a problem is named 'awl. The author in this phrase makes the problem from six. And in one case 'awl occurs up to seven, in the second case up to eight, in the third case up to nine, and in the fourth case up to ten. Their details are coming ahead. The problem runs from six in three cases: (1) the recipient takes one-sixth and remainder, (2) the recipient takes half and one-third, (3) the recipient takes half and one-sixth. Forms of 'awl: The case where the base problem runs from six and the shares become seven is as follows: The deceased left a husband and two full sisters. In this, the husband gets half because there is no child. And two full sisters get two-thirds, therefore the problem runs from six. The problem will be as follows: Deceased 6 'awl 7 Husband Two full sisters 3 In this, the husband gets half i.e. three, and the two sisters get two-thirds i.e. four out of six. Together total becomes seven, so 'awl becomes seven. The calculator calculation will be as follows: Deceased 100 'awl 116.66 Husband After 'awl one share = 116.66 ÷ 100 = 0.8571 Two full sisters Method of 'awl: 66.66 57.13 66.66 x 0.8571 = 57.13 50 x 0.8571 = 42.85 99.98 50 42.85 Two full sisters got after 'awl Husband got after 'awl
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage introduces inheritance cases involving one-sixth (suds), one-half (nisf), and one-third (thuluth) shares. The author states the general rule: when these fractions appear (specifically, 1/6 + remainder, or 1/2 + 1/3, or 1/2 + 1/6), the base number (asl al-mas'alah) is 6. However, sometimes the sum of the fixed shares exceeds the base (1). This is called 'awl (increase). The lexical meaning of 'awl is 'inclination' or 'injustice', as the shares are proportionally reduced to accommodate all heirs. The text explains that 'awl can cause the base to increase from 6 to 7, 8, 9, or 10, depending on the combination. An example is given: a husband and two full sisters. The husband gets 1/2 (3/6), and the two sisters get 2/3 (4/6). Their total is 7/6, which exceeds 1. So the base is increased to 7 (by 'awl), and the shares are recalculated: husband gets 3/7, sisters get 4/7. The text includes a calculator verification showing percentages (e.g., husband's share becomes 42.85% of the estate).

Key Terms
سدس (suds): One-sixth share in inheritance, common for mother or grandfather under certain conditions.
عول ('awl): Proportional increase of the base number (asl al-mas'alah) when fixed shares exceed the estate, causing reduction of all shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of 'awl with a husband and two full sisters, what is the final share of the husband after 'awl?
A) 3/6
B) 3/7
C) 1/2
D) 4/7

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of 'awl ensures equitable distribution when fixed shares exceed the total estate by increasing the base number proportionally.
